This country club is in a beautiful setting.  The course is well cared for.  Security is tight, they take down your license plate and driver license numbers.  They then issue you a computer generated pass.  We had a garden club dinner at one of the resident's home.  They have very nice views of the surrounding mountains.  The drive through the green orange groves is refreshing after seeing the surrounding chaparal<//text>

<review>It's rare when a writer is left speechless, but after my first 90 min session with Brent, I couldn't find a single word to communicate the depth of goodness I felt to the bottom of my bones. The whole session was deeply therapeutic and surpasses any massage I've had before. What Brent does is different than simply massage; he is driving deep into the muscle tissue, down into every nerve cell to push out any trauma and "stuck" energy, instead replacing it with what can only be aptly described as a warm, infinite feeling of pure love. He is a truly gifted healer and I am extraordinarily grateful I was able to visit him after a very serious car accident two weeks prior. Brent advised me on how to listen to the natural intelligence of my body leading up to our session so as to reduce stress and inflammation (no alcohol, no red meat, lots of turmeric, time in the ocean and in my garden, and lots of sleep), which made me feel pretty good at the get-go and enabled Brent to work more deeply to eradicate any tension that lingered.

My only tiff is that I found it unfair to ask me what I thought/felt right after the session... I'm not sure I was able to construct a single coherent thought having been molded into a sort of gelatinous goop, but I tried my best.

Tl;dr: worth every penny. Get on the books sooner rather than later. :) Thanks, Brent!< /review>< gmapID>

I like going here rather than the ER. It is cleaner, you can check-in online and get a wait time. This time however, we had a bad diagnosis. I brought my 12year old son in because he sprained his ankle. He complained of ankle pain but said he couldn‚Äôt feel his foot. I figured we would need x-rays so we headed in. We were seen right away.
The doctor was nice and checked my son‚Äôs ankle. She decided to do ankle x-rays. She came in and said he had a broken heel. I was surprised because he didn‚Äôt mention anything about hitting his heel, just twisting his ankle. She said she and another doctor felt it was very clear his heel was broken but did not know how he got it with the injury my son explained. He was splinted and done up in an ace bandage. I approved charging me for crutches and we were told to follow-up with an orthopedist. She also said the x-ray would be checked with a radiologist. I should receive a call the following day.
Late in the afternoon the next day, she called and said the radiologist thought it was negative for a break but she and her attending were still very convinced. Three days later we decided his heel was clearly not broken. The swelling was down in three days and he was able to walk comfortable on it. On the fifth day, he played in a baseball game. His ankle is still a little sore but our diagnosis was clearly inaccurate. It was disappointing but we are obviously relieved.
I would use this again to avoid the ER for illness but probably not to avoid an x-ray.<//text>

<Review>Tips:
- write your name on the waiting list near the counter
- bring cash

Pros:
- Monte Cristo (savory + sweet. doesn't get much better than that)
- make-your-own omelette (soft, flavorful eggs)
- quick to refill coffee
- they got my mom's order wrong, but re-cooked it, and kept checking on us to make sure she liked it

Cons:
- this place used to be better 5+ years ago; the owner, an elderly man, is still taking orders, but frequently mishears orders which can be frustrating if you have to repeat a complicated order several times
- SUPER crowded (tiny space where tables are crammed together)
- food quality has declined in the last few years

Bottom line: This place is no longer as great as it was during its heyday, but it's still worth eating breakfast here. You should probably go on a weekday to avoid an excessively long wait.<//Review>< Pics>

We brought our very sick cat to the Palmdale VH on Saturday based on all the beautiful reviews, the fact that this hospital is AHHA accredited and it has been in the business since the 80s.
The outcome? Misdiagnoses and malicious charges.
My baby was hospitalized for 3 days, various tests were done, IV fluid with VB were given. He does return home feeling better, but anyone with a little bit knowledge about CKD would know the patient will feel much better with fluid and anti-nausea medicine.
Except received 2 CBC+CHEM+TT4 thyroid tests results and the invoice, we did not have any other lab results or hospital notes. I requested the records 3 times over the phone, 3 times through email request. We were promised to be sent after their lunch break; then pushed to at the time of discharge; then were told after 2 days! Are you serious? You don't need two days to gather the reports, unless you are making fraudulent records or being incompetent in your works! Simply pull up the reports from your system, attach to an email and sent. We paid for them, we are entitled to have the records at the time of discharging. I had never been to a vet not giving us the notes, especially all the lab, tests results at the time of check-out.
We were being told prior the cost can be very expensive, which I expected that, especially they were arrange someone to come in on the closed day to check on him every hour. To the vet's defense, they deserve that. As a pet's owner who has spent over $20k in the past 30-day, we don't have a problem to pay for their works. ONLY if they do what they say.
The vet, the receptionist promised us on the Saturday evening before they close, that a technician would call on Sunday afternoon to give us an update. Sunday came, no call; at 6PM, still no call. So we went to their facility. ABSOLUTELY EMPTY. We were there from 6:30 to 8:30 PM, we didn't see anyone come in. So...what type of 24-hour monitoring you were doing? From Saturday 6PM until Monday 12:20PM, I got absolutely NO update from this facility in 42-hour.
The worst part? The misdiagnoses:
1. My baby came in with history of Diabetes (diagnosed on 12/18/2020) and choric renal failure. Dr. Hanna diagnosed that my baby does not have diabetes, despite his BG readings were in the 300s mg/dl during his stay (based on his statement, I don't have the results yet, so I would not know the true numbers); this statement is all based on one-single Fructosamine test. Of course his BG looks fine on fructosame test, HE HAS BEEN ON INSULIN!!!!!!! He told us DO NOT give my baby any insulin until we go back to see him on Wednesday. When I asked him what if his BG shot over the chart again? His answers? "cats can get very stressful at home", "your home testing results are not as accurate as the clinic" " DO NOT give him any insulin". BS! Studies shown that the home testing is way much less stressful for the pet sand more reliable than the results in the clinic. We use Alphatrak2 meter and authentic Alphatrak supplies, the meter is also calibrated each time according to the code.
2. Infection: we don't see any anti-biotic was given during his stay. His WBC value is 36.18% higher than highest normal value, it went up during his stay. Dr. Hanna? There is no raging infection, it's just a little bit elevated. SERIOUSLY?!< /Text>

i have a couple of cats that have been a regular clients for this vet hosp since 2011. recently they both came down with symptoms of earmites. and i brought 1 in that was showing the strongest signs. because of covid all customer communication is outside in "through the open car window" style. the cat came back with what appeared to be happy to be back with me. cleaned ears as i can see. with some revolution plus treatments (2) to follow up on, and some acetic acid and boric acid ear wash to use, soon i'd imagine. a daily14 day treatment of irrigation of the ear canals, 4 oz bottle. i tried to start that, but the instructions are covered by the vet prescription sticker and the cat went into a itch mode that seemed to be extreme so only 1 side was attempted, with the ears being just cleaned i figure maybe it's best to wait? ears don't look inflamed and they did say upon my asking that the eardrums were not perforated nor torn and i went back to be helped and the same vet assistant, very helpful and clearly informative, only i can't understand nor hear well, not to mention memory is at a serious decline. it would be awesome to have an ability to create and account on the website, not by any of the social media platforms offered, but just an account on their website. that could be a private ability to view and clinical diagnosis', procedures and follow up instructions. so far what i got by asking was there was no ear mites found. but a bacterial infection was suspected or diagnosed i dont' for sure. but other than the Revolution Plus, no antibiotics were mentioned. the cat's conditions have not changed and they are still showing a very high level of itching in the ears and or around the neck. like fleas or flea bites? maybe they've become allergic to something. both onset at the same time. i have no idea of what to look for. they both catch birds and occasional rat that i think live in some palm trees out back. so hope the revolution plus begins to show some results soon. i just know this company could bump up their ratings by having a file access to cases by owners/keepers. the tools are here in the form of technology. only the controversial social media uses to set up an account only invites trouble socially. i'd rather only go between the pet and the vet and myself. facebook...no thanks.</Review>

We took our 7 month old German Shepard puppy in for a double ear infection. Staff was professional and caring. They had trouble treating him due to the pain he was in. They took him in the back and told us they had to give him mild sedation to complete the procedure. When they returned him to us, he was barely walking and had to be carried to the truck.

This past Sunday I had to take my dog to the ER vet since Palmdale vet was closed. The vet at the ER said he had a heart murmur and to follow up with my vet, Dr. McEwan. I took him today and he found no heart murmur. He even asked his fellow vet to also listen to my dogs heart and they both said his heart sounded good. Thank goodness!  I highly recommend Palmdale Vet Hospital. Not only is he an outstanding vet, his office staff is always so friendly and caring. Dawn has always been so helpful, as well as, Christine and all the gals behind the desk!  Thank you everyone!</review>
